<p>As of the census of 2010, there were 129,272 people, 52,471 total households, and 22,638 families residing in the city. The population density was 928.6 people per square mile (358.5/km²). There were 46,142 housing units at an average density of 368.5 per square mile (142.3/km²). The racial makeup of the city was 51.27% <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Non-Hispanic White</a>, 42.20% <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Black</a>, 2.20% <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Asian</a>, 0.25% <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Native American</a>, 0.30% <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Pacific Islander</a>, 1.50% from <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">other races</a>, and 2.00% from two or more races. <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Latino</a> of any race were 4.30% of the population.</p>
<p>There were 45,666 households out of which 22.4% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 28.7% were married couples living together, 17.1% have a female householder with no husband present, and 50.4% were nonfamilies. 38.0% of all households were made up of individuals and 8.9% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.18 and the average family size was 2.94.</p>
<p>In the city, the population was spread out with 20.1% under the age of 18, 22.9% from 18 to 24, 30.1% from 25 to 44, 16.6% from 45 to 64, and 10.3% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 29 years. For every 100 females there were 96.2 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 93.4 males.</p>
<p>The median income for a household in the city was $31,141, and the <a href="/wiki/Median_income" title="Median income">median income</a> for a family was $39,589. Males had a median income of $30,925 versus $24,679 for females. The per capita income for the city was $18,853. About 17.0% of families and 22.1% of the population were below the poverty line, including 29.7% of those under the age of 18 and 16.9% ages 65 or older.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> has 241 congregations and 115,000 members. The <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> has 122 congregations and 51,000 members. The Evangelical Lutheran Church has 71 congregations and 25,400 members. The PC (USA) has 34 congregations and 15,000 members; the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_America" title="Presbyterian Church in America">Presbyterian Church in America</a> has 22 congregations and 8,000 members. The Catholic Church has 14 parishes. There are 3 Jewish synagogues. Muslims are served by the Islamic Center of Columbia, South Carolina.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg/170px-FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg/255px-FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg/340px-FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FirstCitizensBankHQ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/First_Citizens_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="First Citizens Bank">First Citizens Bank</a> building at the corner of Main and Lady streets</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Columbia enjoys a diversified economy, with the major employers in the area being South Carolina state government, the <a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Health" title="Palmetto Health">Palmetto Health</a> hospital system, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Cross_Blue_Shield_of_South_Carolina" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Cross Blue Shield of South Carolina">Blue Cross Blue Shield of South Carolina</a>, Palmetto GBA, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a>. The corporate headquarters of Fortune 1000 energy company, <a href="/wiki/SCANA" title="SCANA">SCANA</a>, are located in the Columbia suburb of Cayce. Other major employers in the Columbia area include <a href="/wiki/Computer_Sciences_Corporation" title="Computer Sciences Corporation">Computer Sciences Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Jackson_(South_Carolina)" title="Fort Jackson (South Carolina)">Fort Jackson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Army" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Army">U.S. Army</a>'s largest and most active initial entry training installation,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> Richland School District One, <a href="/wiki/Humana" title="Humana">Humana</a>/TriCare, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">United Parcel Service</a>, which operates its Southeastern Regional Hub at the Columbia Metropolitan Airport. Major manufacturers such as <a href="/wiki/Square_D" title="Square D">Square D</a>, CMC Steel, Spirax Sarco, <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Paper" title="International Paper">International Paper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pirelli" title="Pirelli">Pirelli</a> Cables, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Electric_Company" title="Westinghouse Electric Company">Westinghouse Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harsco" title="Harsco">Harsco</a> Track Tech, <a href="/wiki/Trane" title="Trane">Trane</a>, Intertape Polymer Group, <a href="/wiki/Union_Switch_%26_Signal" title="Union Switch &amp; Signal">Union Switch &amp; Signal</a>, <a href="/wiki/FN_Herstal" title="FN Herstal">FN Herstal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solectron" title="Solectron">Solectron</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bose_Corporation" title="Bose Corporation">Bose</a> Technology have facilities in the Columbia area. There are over 70 foreign affiliated companies and fourteen <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies in the region. The gross domestic product (GDP) of the Columbia metropolitan statistical area as of 2010 was $31.97 billion, the highest among MSAs in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several companies have their global, continental, or national headquarters in Columbia, including <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Life_%26_Accident_Insurance_Company" title="Colonial Life &amp; Accident Insurance Company">Colonial Life &amp; Accident Insurance Company</a>, the second-largest supplemental insurance company in the nation; the Ritedose Corporation, a <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a> services company; <a href="/wiki/AgFirst" title="AgFirst">AgFirst Farm Credit Bank</a>, the largest bank headquartered in the state with over $30 billion in assets (the non-commercial bank is part of the <a href="/wiki/Farm_Credit_System" title="Farm Credit System">Farm Credit System</a>, the largest agricultural lending organization in the United States which was established by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> in 1916); South State Bank, the largest commercial bank headquartered in South Carolina; <a href="/wiki/Nexsen_Pruet" title="Nexsen Pruet">Nexsen Pruet</a>, LLC, a multi-specialty business law firm in the Carolinas; Spectrum Medical, an international medical software company; Wilbur Smith Associates, a full-service transportation and infrastructure consulting firm; and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mullins" class="mw-redirect" title="Nelson Mullins">Nelson Mullins</a>, a major national law firm. CSC's Financial Services Group, a major provider of software and outsourcing services to the insurance industry, is headquartered in the Columbia suburb of Blythewood.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_revitalization">Downtown revitalization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Downtown revitalization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Street_edited.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lady_Street_edited.jpg/220px-Lady_Street_edited.jpg" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lady_Street_edited.jpg/330px-Lady_Street_edited.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lady_Street_edited.jpg/440px-Lady_Street_edited.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2036" data-file-height="784" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Street_edited.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lady Street in the historic <a href="/wiki/Congaree_Vista" title="Congaree Vista">Congaree Vista</a> district downtown</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Columbia has recently accomplished a number of urban redevelopment projects and has several more planned.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> The historic <a href="/wiki/Congaree_Vista" title="Congaree Vista">Congaree Vista</a>, a 1,200-acre (5&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) district running from the central business district toward the Congaree River, features a number of historic buildings that have been rehabilitated since its revitalization begun in the late 1980s. Of note is the <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_reuse" title="Adaptive reuse">adaptive reuse</a> of the Confederate Printing Plant on Gervais and Huger, used to print Confederate bills during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. The city cooperated with <a href="/wiki/Publix" title="Publix">Publix</a> grocery stores to preserve the look. This won Columbia an award from the International Downtown Association.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> The Vista district is also where the region's convention center and anchor <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilton Hotels">Hilton</a> hotel with a <a href="/wiki/Ruth%27s_Chris_Steakhouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruth's Chris Steakhouse">Ruth's Chris Steakhouse</a> restaurant are located. Other notable developments under construction and recently completed include high-end condos and townhomes, hotels, and mixed-use structures.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MainStreetbanner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/MainStreetbanner.jpg/170px-MainStreetbanner.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/MainStreetbanner.jpg/255px-MainStreetbanner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/MainStreetbanner.jpg/340px-MainStreetbanner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MainStreetbanner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A downtown lightpost banner heralds Columbia's "New Main Street" as part of an effort to reinfuse life and vitality into Main Street.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The older buildings lining the Vista's main thoroughfare, Gervais Street, now house art galleries, restaurants, unique shops, and professional office space. Near the end of Gervais is the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_Museum" title="South Carolina State Museum">South Carolina State Museum</a> and the EdVenture Children's Museum. Private student housing and some residential projects are going up nearby; the CanalSide development<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> at the site of the old Central Correctional Institution, is the most high-profile. At full build-out, the development will have 750 residential units and provides access to Columbia's waterfront. Lady Street between Huger and Assembly streets in the Vista and the <a href="/wiki/Five_Points_(Columbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Five Points (Columbia)">Five Points neighborhood</a> have undergone beautification projects, which mainly consisted of replacing curbs and gutters, and adding brick-paved sidewalks and angled parking.</p>
<p>Special revitalization efforts are being aimed at Main Street, which began seeing an exodus of department and specialty stores in the 1990s. The goal is to re-establish Main Street as a vibrant commercial and residential corridor, and the stretch of Main Street home to most businesses—-from Gervais to Blanding streets—-has been streetscaped in recent years. Notable developments completed in recent years along Main Street include an 18-story, $60 million tower at the high-profile corner of Main and Gervais streets, the renovation of the 1441 Main Street office building as the new Midlands headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> Bank (formerly <a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a> Bank), a new sanctuary for the Holy Trinity <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox">Greek Orthodox</a> Church, the location of Mast General store in the historic <a href="/wiki/Efird%27s_Department_Store" title="Efird's Department Store">Efird's building</a>, and the relocation of the Nickelodeon theater. A façade improvement program for the downtown business district, implemented in 2011, has resulted in the restoration and improvement of the façades of several historic Main Street shopfronts. One of the most ambitious development projects in the city's history is currently underway which involves old state mental health campus downtown on Bull Street. Known formally as Columbia Common, this project will consist of rehabbing several historic buildings on the campus for residential, hospitality, and retail use.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> A new minor league baseball stadium was recently built on the campus as well.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg/220px-ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg/330px-ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg/440px-ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2044" data-file-height="1228" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ColumbiaMuseumofArt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Columbia_Museum_of_Art" title="Columbia Museum of Art">Columbia Museum of Art</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EdVenture.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/EdVenture.jpg/220px-EdVenture.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/EdVenture.jpg/330px-EdVenture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/EdVenture.jpg/440px-EdVenture.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1227" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EdVenture.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/EdVenture" title="EdVenture">EdVenture</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Town Theatre is the country's oldest community theatre in continuous use. Located a block from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> campus, its playhouse is listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. Since 1917, the theatre has produced plays and musicals of wide general appeal.</li>
<li>Trustus Theatre is Columbia's professional theatre company. Founded more than 20 years ago, Trustus brought a new dimension to theatre in South Carolina's capital city. Patrons have the opportunity to watch new shows directly from the stages of New York as well as classic shows rarely seen in Columbia.</li>
<li>The Nickelodeon Theater is a 99-seat store front theater located on Main Street between Taylor and Blanding Streets. In operation since 1979, "the Nick", run by the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Film_Society" title="Columbia Film Society">Columbia Film Society</a>, is home to two film screenings each evening and an additional matinée three days a week. The Nick is the only non-profit art house film theater in South Carolina and is the home for 25,000 filmgoers each year.</li>
<li>Columbia Marionette Theatre has the distinction of being the only free standing theatre in the nation devoted entirely to marionette arts.</li>
<li>The South Carolina Shakespeare Company performs the plays of <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> and other classical works throughout the state.</li>
<li>Workshop Theatre of South Carolina opened in 1967 as a place where area directors could practice their craft. The theatre produces musicals and Broadway fare and also brings new theatrical material to Columbia.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_Museum" title="South Carolina State Museum">The South Carolina State Museum</a> is a comprehensive museum with exhibits in science, technology, history, and the arts. It is the state's largest museum and one of the largest museums in the Southeast.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Museum_of_Art" title="Columbia Museum of Art">Columbia Museum of Art</a> features changing exhibits throughout the year. Located at the corner of Hampton and Main Streets, the museum offers art, lectures, films, and guided tours.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EdVenture" title="EdVenture">EdVenture</a> is one of the South's largest children's museums and the second largest in South Carolina. It is located next to the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_Museum" title="South Carolina State Museum">South Carolina State Museum</a> on Gervais Street. The museum allows children to explore and learn while having fun.</li>
<li>McKissick Museum is located on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> campus. The museum features changing exhibitions of art, science, regional history, and folk art.</li>
<li>The Confederate Relic Room and Military Museum showcases an artifact collection from the Colonial period to the space age. The museum houses a diverse collection of artifacts from the South Carolina confederate period.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Richland_County_Public_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="The Richland County Public Library">The Richland County Public Library</a>, named the 2001 National Library of the Year, serves area citizens through its main library and nine branches. The 242,000-square-foot (22,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) main library has a large book collection, provides reference services, utilizes the latest technology, houses a children's collection, and displays artwork.</li>
<li>The South Carolina State Library provides library services to all citizens of South Carolina through the interlibrary loan service utilized by the public libraries located in each county.</li>
<li>The Columbia City Ballet is Columbia's ballet company, offering more than 80 major performances annually. Artistic director William Starrett, formerly of the Joffrey Ballet and American Ballet Theatre, runs the company.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Philharmonic" title="South Carolina Philharmonic">South Carolina Philharmonic Orchestra</a> is Columbia's resident orchestra. The Philharmonic produces a full season of orchestral performances each year. Renowned musicians come to Columbia to perform as guest artists with the orchestra.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> In April 2008 <a href="/wiki/Morihiko_Nakahara" title="Morihiko Nakahara">Morihiko Nakahara</a> was named the new Music Director of the Philharmonic.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Columbia_City_Jazz_Dance_Company" title="Columbia City Jazz Dance Company">Columbia City Jazz Dance Company</a>, formed in 1990 by artistic director Dale Lam, was named one of the "Top 50 Dance Companies in the USA" by Dance Spirit magazine. Columbia City Jazz specializes in modern, lyrical, and percussive jazz dance styles and has performed locally, regionally, and nationally in exhibitions, competitions, community functions, and international tours in Singapore, <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a>, Bulgaria, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Palmetto Opera debuted in 2003 with a performance of "Love, Murder &amp; Revenge," a mixture of scenes from famous operas. The organization's mission is to present professional opera to the Midlands and South Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Columbia Choral Society has been performing throughout the community since 1930. Under the direction of Dr. William Carswell, the group strives to stimulate and broaden interest in musical activities and to actively engage in the rehearsal and rendition of choral music.</li>
<li>Alternacirque is a professional circus that produces variety shows and full-scale themed productions. Formed in 2007, Alternacirque is directed by Natalie Brown.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pocket Productions is an arts organization devoted to inspiring and expanding the arts community in Columbia, SC, through ArtRageous,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> Playing After Dark<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> and other community-based collaborative events.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Movies filmed in the Columbia area include <a href="/wiki/The_Program_(1993_film)" title="The Program (1993 film)">The Program</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Man_(film)" title="Renaissance Man (film)">Renaissance Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chasers" title="Chasers">Chasers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death_Sentence_(2007_film)" title="Death Sentence (2007 film)">Death Sentence</a>, <a href="/wiki/A_Guy_Named_Joe" title="A Guy Named Joe">A Guy Named Joe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Accidental_Love" title="Accidental Love">Accidental Love</a>/Nailed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/10/Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg/220px-Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/10/Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg/330px-Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/10/Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg/440px-Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1136" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cola_Met_Conv_Cntr.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Columbia Metropolitan Convention Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Columbia_Metropolitan_Convention_Center">Columbia Metropolitan Convention Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Columbia Metropolitan Convention Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Columbia Metropolitan Convention, which opened in September 2004 as South Carolina's only downtown convention center,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> is a 142,500-square-foot (13,240&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), modern, state-of-the-art facility designed to host a variety of meetings and conventions. Located in the historic Congaree Vista district, this facility is close to restaurants, antique and specialty shops, art galleries, and various popular nightlife venues. The main exhibit hall contains almost 25,000 square feet (2,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space; the Columbia Ballroom over 18,000 square feet (1,700&#160;m<sup>2</sup>); and the five meeting rooms ranging in size from 1500 to 4,000 square feet (400&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) add another 15,000 square feet (1,400&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space. The facility is located next to the Colonial Life Arena.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Koger_Center_for_the_Arts">Koger Center for the Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Koger Center for the Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Koger_Center_for_the_Arts" title="Koger Center for the Arts">Koger Center for the Arts</a> provides Columbia with theatre, music, and dance performances that range from local acts to global acts.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> The facility seats 2,256 persons. The center is named for philanthropists Ira and Nancy Koger, who made a substantial donation from personal and corporate funds for construction of the $15 million center. The first performance at the Koger Center was given by the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a> and took place on Saturday, January 14, 1989. The facility is known for hosting diverse events, from the State of the State Address to the South Carolina Body Building Championship and the South Carolina Science Fair.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Carolina_Coliseum">Carolina Coliseum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Carolina Coliseum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CarolinaColiseum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinaColiseum.jpg/220px-CarolinaColiseum.jpg" width="220" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinaColiseum.jpg/330px-CarolinaColiseum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinaColiseum.jpg/440px-CarolinaColiseum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="1449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CarolinaColiseum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Coliseum" title="Carolina Coliseum">Carolina Coliseum</a> facing Assembly St.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carolina_Coliseum" title="Carolina Coliseum">Carolina Coliseum</a>, which opened in 1968, is a 12,401-seat facility which initially served as the home of the USC Gamecocks' basketball teams. The arena could be easily adapted to serve other entertainment purposes, including concerts, car shows, circuses, ice shows, and other popular events. The versatility and quality of the coliseum at one time allowed the university to use the facility for performing arts events such as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Pops" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Pops">Boston Pops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Symphony" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Symphony">Chicago Symphony</a>, Feld Ballet, and other performances by important artists. An acoustical shell and a state-of-the-art lighting system assisted the coliseum in presenting such activities. The coliseum was the home of the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Inferno" title="Columbia Inferno">Columbia Inferno</a>, an <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">ECHL</a> team. However, since the construction of the Colonial Life Arena in 2002, the coliseum is no longer used for basketball, but is still used as classroom space for the Schools of Journalism and Hospitality, Retail, and Sport Management.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Township_Auditorium">Township Auditorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Township Auditorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Township Auditorium seats 3,099 capacity and is located in downtown Columbia. The <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian Revival</a> building was designed by the Columbia architectural firm of Lafaye and Lafaye and constructed in 1930. The Township has hosted thousands of events from concerts to conventions to wrestling matches. The auditorium was listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> on September 28, 2005, and has recently undergone a $12 million extensive interior and exterior renovation.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</ol>
</div>
<p>The most popular sports in Columbia are the sports programs at the University of South Carolina. Columbia also offers minor league, semi-pro, and amateur sports.</p>
<p>Columbia has also hosted the women's U.S. Olympic Marathon Trials in 1996 and 2000<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> and the 2007 Junior Wildwater World Championships, which featured many European canoe and kayak racers.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> The Colonial Life Arena has also hosted <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> exhibition games.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_venues">Sports venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sports venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Williams-Brice_Stadium" title="Williams-Brice Stadium">Williams-Brice Stadium</a> is the home of the USC Gamecocks' football team and is the 24th largest college football stadium in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> It seats 80,250 people and is located just south of downtown Columbia. The stadium was built in 1934 with the help of federal Works Progress Administration funds, and initially seated 17,600. The original name was Carolina Stadium, but on September 9, 1972, it was renamed to honor the Williams and Brice families. Mrs. Martha Williams-Brice had left much of her estate to the university for stadium renovations and expansions. Her late husband, Thomas H. Brice, played football for the university from 1922 to 1924.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ColonialLifeArena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ColonialLifeArena.jpg/220px-ColonialLifeArena.jpg" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ColonialLifeArena.jpg/330px-ColonialLifeArena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ColonialLifeArena.jpg/440px-ColonialLifeArena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2040" data-file-height="972" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ColonialLifeArena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Colonial_Life_Arena" title="Colonial Life Arena">Colonial Life Arena</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colonial_Life_Arena" title="Colonial Life Arena">Colonial Life Arena</a>, opened in 2002, is Columbia's premier arena and entertainment facility.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Seating 18,000 for college basketball, it is the largest arena in the state of South Carolina,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and the tenth largest on-campus basketball facility in the nation,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> serving as the home of the men's and women's USC Gamecocks basketball teams. Located on the University of South Carolina campus, this facility features 41 suites, four entertainment suites, and the Frank McGuire Club, a full-service hospitality room with a capacity of 300. The facility has padded seating, a sound system, and a four-sided video scoreboard.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The $13 million <a href="/wiki/Charlie_W._Johnson_Stadium" title="Charlie W. Johnson Stadium">Charlie W. Johnson Stadium</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Benedict_College" title="Benedict College">Benedict College</a> football and soccer. The structure was completed and dedicated in 2006 and seats 11,000 with a maximum capacity of 16,000.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Founders_Park" title="Founders Park">Founders Park</a> opened in 2009. Seating 8,400 permanently for college baseball and an additional 1,000 for standing room only, it is the largest baseball stadium in the state of South Carolina,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and serves as the home of the University of South Carolina Gamecocks' baseball team. Located near Granby Park near downtown Columbia, this facility features entertainment suites, a picnic terrace, and a dining deck. The facility also features a sound system and scoreboard.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 6, 2015, developers broke ground on the $37 million <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Communications_Park" title="Spirit Communications Park">Spirit Communications Park</a>. The stadium is the home for the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Fireflies" title="Columbia Fireflies">Columbia Fireflies</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a> team playing in the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_League" title="South Atlantic League">South Atlantic League</a>. It opened in April 2016 and can seat up to 7,501 people. Columbia had been without minor league baseball since the <a href="/wiki/Capital_City_Bombers" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital City Bombers">Capital City Bombers</a> relocated to <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_South_Carolina" title="Greenville, South Carolina">Greenville, South Carolina</a>, in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-milb_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milb-52">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FinlayPark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FinlayPark.jpg/220px-FinlayPark.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FinlayPark.jpg/330px-FinlayPark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FinlayPark.jpg/440px-FinlayPark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FinlayPark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Finlay_Park" title="Finlay Park">Finlay Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region's most popular park,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Finlay_Park" title="Finlay Park">Finlay Park</a> has hosted just about everything from festivals and political rallies to road races and Easter Sunrise services. This 18-acre (73,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) park has had two lives; first dedicated in 1859 as Sidney Park, named in honor of Algernon Sidney Johnson, a Columbia City Councilman, the park experienced an illustrious but short tenure. The park fell into disrepair after the Civil War and served as a site for commercial ventures until the late 20th century. In 1990, the park was reopened. It serves as the site for such events as Kids Day, The Summer Concert Series, plus many more activities. In 1992, the park was renamed Finlay Park, in honor of Kirkman Finlay, a past mayor of Columbia who had a vision to reenergize the historic Congaree Vista district, between Main Street and the river, and recreate the site that was formerly known as Sidney Park.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Memorial_Park.jpg/220px-Memorial_Park.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Memorial_Park.jpg/330px-Memorial_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Memorial_Park.jpg/440px-Memorial_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1451" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Memorial Park is a 4-acre (16,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) tract of land in the Congaree Vista between Main Street and the river. The property is bordered by Hampton, Gadsden, Washington, and Wayne Streets and is one block south of Finlay Park. This park was created to serve as a memorial to those who served their country and presently has monuments honoring the <a href="/wiki/USS_Columbia" title="USS Columbia">USS Columbia</a> warship and those that served with her during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the China-Burma-India Theater Veterans of WWII, casualties of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> attack of December 7, 1941, who were from South Carolina, <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_survivors" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust survivors">Holocaust survivors</a> who live in South Carolina as well as concentration camp liberators from South Carolina, and the State <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> Veterans. The park was dedicated in November 1986 along with the unveiling of the South Carolina Vietnam Monument. In June 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> Memorial was dedicated at Memorial Park. In November 2014, Columbia native and resident of Boston, Henry Crede, gave a bronze statue and plaza in the park dedicated to his WWII comrades who served in the Navy from South Carolina.</p>
<p>Granby Park opened in November 1998 as a gateway to the rivers of Columbia, adding another access to the many river activities available to residents. Granby is part of the Three Rivers Greenway, a system of green spaces along the banks of the rivers in Columbia, adding another piece to the long-range plan and eventually connecting to the existing Riverfront Park. Granby is a 24-acre (97,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) linear park with canoe access points, fishing spots, bridges, and ½ mile of nature trail along the banks of the Congaree River.</p>
<p>In the Five Points district of downtown Columbia is the park dedicated to the legacy and memory of the most celebrated civil rights leader in America, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a> Park. Formerly known as Valley Park, it was historically known to be largely restricted to Whites. Renaming the park after Martin Luther King Jr. in the late 1980s was seen as a progressive and unifying event on behalf of the city, civic groups, and local citizens. The park features a beautiful water sculpture and a community center. An integral element of the park is the Stone of Hope monument, unveiled in January 1996. Upon the monument is inscribed a portion of King's 1964 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> acceptance speech: "History is cluttered with the wreckage of nations and individuals that pursued that self-defeating path of hate. Love is the key to the solutions of the problems of the world."</p>
<p>One of Columbia's greatest assets is <a href="/wiki/Riverbanks_Zoo" title="Riverbanks Zoo">Riverbanks Zoo &amp; Garden</a>. Riverbanks Zoo is a sanctuary for more than 2,000 animals housed in natural habitat exhibits along the Saluda River. Just across the river, the 70-acre (280,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) botanical garden is devoted to gardens, woodlands, plant collections, and historic ruins. Riverbanks has been named one of America's best zoos<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> and the No. 1 travel attraction in the Southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> It attracted over one million visitors in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Situated along the meandering Congaree River in central South Carolina, <a href="/wiki/Congaree_National_Park" title="Congaree National Park">Congaree National Park</a> is home to champion trees, primeval forest landscapes, and diverse plant and animal life. This 22,200-acre (90&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) park protects the largest contiguous tract of old-growth bottomland hardwood forest remaining in the United States. The park is an international <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere reserve">biosphere reserve</a>. Known for its giant hardwoods and towering pines, the park's floodplain forest includes one of the highest canopies in the world and some of the tallest trees in the eastern United States. Congaree National Park provides a sanctuary for plants and animals, a research site for scientists, and a place to walk and relax in a tranquil wilderness setting.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sesquicentennial_State_Park" title="Sesquicentennial State Park">Sesquicentennial State Park</a> is a 1,419-acre (6&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) park, featuring a beautiful 30-acre (120,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) lake surrounded by trails and picnic areas. The park's proximity to downtown Columbia and three major interstate highways attracts both local residents and travelers. Sesquicentennial is often the site of family reunions and group campouts. Interpretive nature programs are a major attraction to the park. The park also contains a two-story log house, dating back to the mid 18th century, which was relocated to the park in 1969. This house is believed to be the oldest building still standing in Richland County. The park was originally built by the Civilian Conservation Corps in the 1930s. Evidence of their craftsmanship is still present today.</p>
<p>In November 1996, the River Alliance proposed that a 12-mile (19&#160;km) linear park system be created to link people to their rivers. This was named the Three Rivers Greenway, and the $18 million estimated cost was agreed to by member governments (the cities of <a href="/wiki/Cayce,_South_Carolina" title="Cayce, South Carolina">Cayce</a>, Columbia, and <a href="/wiki/West_Columbia,_South_Carolina" title="West Columbia, South Carolina">West Columbia</a>) with the proviso that the Alliance recommend an acceptable funding strategy.</p>
<p>While the funding process was underway, an existing city of Columbia site located on the <a href="/wiki/Congaree_River" title="Congaree River">Congaree River</a> offered an opportunity to be a pilot project for the Three Rivers Greenway. The Alliance was asked to design and permit for construction by a general contractor this component. This approximately one-half-mile segment of the system was opened in November 1998. It is complete with 8-foot (2.4&#160;m) wide concrete pathways, vandal-proof lighting, trash receptacles, water fountains, picnic benches, overlooks, bank fishing access, canoe/kayak access, a public restroom and parking. These set the standards for the common elements in the rest of the system. Eventually, pathways will run from Granby to the Riverbanks Zoo. Boaters, sportspeople, and fisherpeople will have access to the area, and additional recreational uses are being planned along the miles of riverfront.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg/220px-EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg/330px-EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg/440px-EsplanadeatCanalside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="350" /></a>

Esplanade at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Canal" title="Columbia Canal">Columbia Canal</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg/220px-Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg/330px-Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg/440px-Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_Murray_B0078.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lake_Murray_(South_Carolina)" title="Lake Murray (South Carolina)">Lake Murray Dam</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Running beside the historic <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Canal" title="Columbia Canal">Columbia Canal</a>, Riverfront Park hosts a two and a half-mile trail. Spanning the canal is an old railway bridge that now is a pedestrian walkway. The park is popular for walking, running, bicycling, and fishing. <a href="/wiki/Picnic_table" title="Picnic table">Picnic tables</a> and benches dot the walking trail. Markers are located along the trail so that visitors can measure distance. The park is part of the Palmetto Trail, a hiking and biking trail that stretches the entire length of the state, from <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_South_Carolina" title="Greenville, South Carolina">Greenville</a> to <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a>.</p>
<p>Other parks in the Columbia area include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/W._Gordon_Belser_Arboretum" title="W. Gordon Belser Arboretum">W. Gordon Belser Arboretum</a></li>
<li>Maxcy Gregg Park</li>
<li>Hyatt Park</li>
<li>Earlewood Park</li>
<li>Granby Park</li>
<li>Owens Field Park</li>
<li>Guignard Park</li>
<li>Southeast Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harbison_State_Forest" title="Harbison State Forest">Harbison State Forest</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbia,_SC,_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG/220px-Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG/330px-Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG/440px-Columbia%2C_SC%2C_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbia,_SC,_City_Hall_IMG_4807.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Columbia City Hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Columbia has a <a href="/wiki/Council-manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Council-manager">council-manager</a> form of government. The mayor and <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> are elected every four years, with no <a href="/wiki/Term_limit" title="Term limit">term limits</a>. Elections are held in the spring of even numbered years. Unlike other mayors in council-manager systems, the Columbia mayor has the power to veto <a href="/wiki/Local_ordinance" title="Local ordinance">ordinances</a> passed by the council; vetoes can be overridden by a two-thirds majority of the council, which appoints a <a href="/wiki/City_manager" title="City manager">city manager</a> to serve as chief administrative officer. The current mayor is <a href="/wiki/Stephen_K._Benjamin" title="Stephen K. Benjamin">Stephen K. Benjamin</a>, who succeeded longtime mayor and fellow Democrat <a href="/wiki/Bob_Coble" title="Bob Coble">Bob Coble</a> in 2010. Teresa Wilson is the current city manager.</p>
<p>The city council consists of six members, four from districts and two elected <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a>. The city council is responsible for making policies and enacting laws, rules, and regulations in order to provide for future community and economic growth, in addition to providing the necessary support for the orderly and efficient operation of city services.</p>
<p><b>At-Large</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Tameika Isaac Devine</li>
<li>Howard Duvall Jr.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Districts</b></p>
<ul>
<li>1: Sam Davis</li>
<li>2: Edward McDowell, Jr.</li>
<li>3: Moe Baddourah</li>
<li>4: Daniel J. Rikenmann</li>
</ul>
<p><i>See related article <a href="/wiki/Past_mayors_of_Columbia,_South_Carolina" class="mw-redirect" title="Past mayors of Columbia, South Carolina">Past mayors of Columbia, South Carolina</a></i></p>
<p>The city's police force is the Columbia Police Department. The chief of police answers to the city manager. Presently, the chief of police is W.H. "Skip" Holbrook; Holbrook was sworn in on April 11, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Department_of_Corrections" title="South Carolina Department of Corrections">South Carolina Department of Corrections</a>, headquartered in Columbia,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> operates several correctional facilities in Columbia. They include the <a href="/wiki/Broad_River_Correctional_Institution" title="Broad River Correctional Institution">Broad River Correctional Institution</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> the Goodman Correctional Institution,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Camille_Griffin_Graham_Correctional_Institution" title="Camille Griffin Graham Correctional Institution">Camille Griffin Graham Correctional Institution</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> the Stevenson Correctional Institution,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> and the Campbell Pre-Release Center.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> Graham houses the state's female death row.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> The state of South Carolina's execution chamber is located at Broad River. From 1990 to 1997, Broad River housed the state's male death row.<sup id="cite_ref-Deathrow_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deathrow-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_installations">Military installations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military installations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Jackson_(South_Carolina)" title="Fort Jackson (South Carolina)">Fort Jackson</a> is the U.S. Army's largest training post.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/McEntire_Joint_National_Guard_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="McEntire Joint National Guard Station">McEntire Joint National Guard Station</a> is under command of the South Carolina Air National Guard.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Columbia is home to the main campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a>, which was chartered in 1801 as South Carolina College and in 1906 as the University of South Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> The university has 350 degree programs and enrolls 31,964 students throughout fifteen degree-granting colleges and schools.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> It is an urban university, located in downtown Columbia.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Usc_horseshoe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Usc_horseshoe.jpg/220px-Usc_horseshoe.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Usc_horseshoe.jpg/330px-Usc_horseshoe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Usc_horseshoe.jpg/440px-Usc_horseshoe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Usc_horseshoe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ohio_Stadium" title="Ohio Stadium">The Horseshoe</a> at USC</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Columbia is also home to:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Allen_University" title="Allen University">Allen University</a> – Allen University was founded in 1870 by the <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">African Methodist Episcopal Church</a>. Allen University is accredited by the Commission on Colleges of the Southern Association of Colleges and Schools (SACS) to award baccalaureate degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Benedict_College" title="Benedict College">Benedict College</a> – Founded in 1870, Benedict is an independent coeducational college. Benedict is one of the fastest growing of the 39 <a href="/wiki/United_Negro_College_Fund" title="United Negro College Fund">United Negro College Fund</a> schools. In addition to an increase in enrollment, Benedict has also seen an increase in average SAT scores, Honors College enrollee rates, capital giving dollars, and the number of research grants awarded. Recently, Benedict has been subject to a series of recent controversies, including basing up to 60 percent of grades solely on effort,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> which have nearly resulted in its losing its <a href="/wiki/Accreditation" title="Accreditation">accreditation</a>. However, in recent months the college has improved its financial standing and is seeking to boost its enrollment.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Columbia_College_(Columbia,_South_Carolina)" class="mw-redirect" title="Columbia College (Columbia, South Carolina)">Columbia College</a> – Founded in 1854, Columbia College is a private, four-year, liberal arts college for women with a coeducational Evening College and Graduate School. The college has been ranked since 1994 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a> as one of the top ten regional liberal arts colleges in the South.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Columbia_International_University" title="Columbia International University">Columbia International University</a> is a biblically based, private Christian institution committed to "preparing men and women to know Christ and to make Him known."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ECPI_University" title="ECPI University">ECPI University</a> has specialized in student-centered technology, business, criminal justice, and health science for 47 years – A leading private university offering master's, bachelor's, associate degree and diploma programs. Continuing Education certification programs are also available. ECPI University is accredited by the Commission on Colleges of the Southern Association of Colleges and Schools to award associate, baccalaureate, and master's degrees and diploma programs. ECPI University Columbia campus also has programmatic accreditation for Medical Assisting with the Accrediting Bureau of Health Education Schools.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Theological_Southern_Seminary" title="Lutheran Theological Southern Seminary">Lutheran Theological Southern Seminary</a> – This institution, founded in 1830, is a seminary of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">Evangelical Lutheran Church in America</a>. One of the oldest Lutheran seminaries in North America, Southern is a fully accredited graduate school of theology preparing women and men for the ordained and lay ministries of the church. The wooded 17-acre (69,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) campus is situated atop Seminary Ridge in Columbia, the highest point in the Midlands area, near the geographic center of the city.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midlands_Technical_College" title="Midlands Technical College">Midlands Technical College</a> – Midlands Tech is part of the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Technical_College_System" title="South Carolina Technical College System">South Carolina Technical College System</a>. It is a two-year, comprehensive, public, community college, offering a wide variety of programs in career education, four-year college-transfer options, and continuing education. Small classes, individualized instruction, and student support services are provided. Most of the college's teaching faculty holds master's or doctoral degrees.</li>
<li>Fortis College<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> – Fortis College is part of the Educational Affiliates Inc, and offers many different career-based degrees.</li>
<li>South Carolina School of Leadership – Established in 2006, South Carolina School of Leadership (SCSL) is a post-secondary "<a href="/wiki/Gap_year" title="Gap year">gap year</a>" school with an intense focus on Christian discipleship and leadership development.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> SCSL uses curriculum from <a href="/wiki/Valley_Forge_Christian_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Valley Forge Christian College">Valley Forge Christian College</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virginia_College" title="Virginia College">Virginia College</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> – Virginia College received senior college recognition from the Accrediting Council for Independent Colleges and Schools (ACICS) which now accredits all programs at the school's campuses</li>
</ul>
<p>Columbia is also the site of several extension campuses, including those for <a href="/wiki/Erskine_Theological_Seminary" title="Erskine Theological Seminary">Erskine Theological Seminary</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_University" title="South University">South University</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Phoenix" title="University of Phoenix">University of Phoenix</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_school_districts">Public school districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Public school districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richland_County_School_District_One" title="Richland County School District One">Richland County School District One</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richland_County_School_District_Two" title="Richland County School District Two">Richland County School District Two</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Columbia's daily newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_State_(newspaper)" title="The State (newspaper)">The State</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> and <i>Cola Daily</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> and its alternative newspapers include <i>Free Times</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> <i>The Columbia Star</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> <i>Carolina Panorama Newspaper</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> and <i>SC Black News</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Columbia Metropolitan Magazine</i><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> is a bi-monthly publication about news and events in the metropolitan area. <i>Greater Columbia Business Monthly</i><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> highlights economic development, business, education, and the arts. <i><a href="/wiki/Q-Notes" title="Q-Notes">Q-Notes</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> a bi-weekly newspaper serving the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community and published in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>, is distributed to locations in Columbia and via home delivery.</p>
<p>Columbia is home to the headquarters and production facilities of <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Educational_Television" title="South Carolina Educational Television">South Carolina Educational Television</a> and South Carolina Public Radio, the state's <a href="/wiki/Public_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Public television">public television</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Public radio">public radio</a> networks.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Columbia has the 78th largest television market in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> Network affiliates include <a href="/wiki/WIS" title="WIS">WIS</a> (<a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>), <a href="/wiki/WLTX" title="WLTX">WLTX</a> (<a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>), <a href="/wiki/WACH" title="WACH">WACH</a> (<a href="/wiki/FOX" class="mw-redirect" title="FOX">FOX</a>) and <a href="/wiki/WOLO-TV" title="WOLO-TV">WOLO</a> (<a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_transit">Mass transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mass transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Comet_(transit)" title="The Comet (transit)">The Comet</a>, officially the Central Midlands Regional Transit Authority, is the agency responsible for operating mass transit in the greater Columbia area including <a href="/wiki/Cayce,_South_Carolina" title="Cayce, South Carolina">Cayce</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Columbia,_South_Carolina" title="West Columbia, South Carolina">West Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest_Acres" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest Acres">Forest Acres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_Lakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Arcadia Lakes">Arcadia Lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Springdale,_Lexington_County,_South_Carolina" title="Springdale, Lexington County, South Carolina">Springdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_South_Carolina" title="Lexington, South Carolina">Lexington</a> <sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup> and the St. Andrews area. COMET operates express shuttles, as well as bus service serving Columbia and its immediate suburbs. The authority was established in October 2002 after SCANA released ownership of public transportation back to the city of Columbia. Since 2003, COMET has provided transportation for more than 2 million passengers, has expanded route services, and introduced 43 new ADA accessible buses offering a safer, more comfortable means of transportation. CMRTA has also added 10 natural gas powered buses to the fleet. COMET went under a name change and rebranding project in 2013. Before then, the system was called the Columbia Metropolitan Rapid Transit Association or "CMRTA".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Central Midlands Council of Governments is in the process of investigating the potential for rail transit in the region. Routes into downtown Columbia originating from Camden, Newberry, and Batesburg-Leesville are in consideration, as is a potential line between Columbia and Charlotte connecting the two mainlines of the future Southeastern High Speed Rail Corridor.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_highways">Roads and highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Roads and highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Columbia's central location between the population centers of South Carolina has made it a transportation focal point with three interstate highways and one interstate spur.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Interstates">Interstates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Interstates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:I-26_(SC).svg" class="image"><img alt="I-26 (SC).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/20px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/30px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/40px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="601" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_26_in_South_Carolina" title="Interstate 26 in South Carolina">I-26</a> Interstate 26 travels from northwest to southeast and connects Columbia to the other two major population centers of South Carolina: the Greenville-Spartanburg area in the northwestern part of the state and <a href="/wiki/North_Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="North Charleston, South Carolina">North Charleston</a> – Charleston area in the southeastern part of the state. It also serves the nearby towns and suburbs of Chapin, Irmo, Harbison, Gaston, and Swansea.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:I-20_(SC).svg" class="image"><img alt="I-20 (SC).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/I-20_%28SC%29.svg/20px-I-20_%28SC%29.svg.png" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/I-20_%28SC%29.svg/30px-I-20_%28SC%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/I-20_%28SC%29.svg/40px-I-20_%28SC%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="601" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_20_in_South_Carolina" title="Interstate 20 in South Carolina">I-20</a> Interstate 20 travels from west to east and connects Columbia to Atlanta and Augusta in the west and Florence in the east. It serves the nearby towns and suburbs of Pelion, Lexington, West Columbia, Sandhill, Pontiac, and Elgin. Interstate 20 is also used by travelers heading to Myrtle Beach, although the interstate's eastern terminus is in Florence.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:I-77_(SC).svg" class="image"><img alt="I-77 (SC).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/I-77_%28SC%29.svg/20px-I-77_%28SC%29.svg.png" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/I-77_%28SC%29.svg/30px-I-77_%28SC%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/I-77_%28SC%29.svg/40px-I-77_%28SC%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="601" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_77_in_South_Carolina" title="Interstate 77 in South Carolina">I-77</a> Interstate 77 begins at a junction with Interstate 26 south of Columbia and travels north to Rock Hill and Charlotte. This interstate also provides direct access to Fort Jackson, the U.S. Army's largest training base and one of Columbia's largest employers. It serves the nearby towns and suburbs of Forest Acres, Gadsden, and Blythewood.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:I-126_(SC).svg" class="image"><img alt="I-126 (SC).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/I-126_%28SC%29.svg/25px-I-126_%28SC%29.svg.png" width="25" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/I-126_%28SC%29.svg/38px-I-126_%28SC%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/I-126_%28SC%29.svg/50px-I-126_%28SC%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="751" data-file-height="601" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_126" title="Interstate 126">I-126</a> Interstate 126 begins downtown at Elmwood Avenue and travels west towards Interstate 26 and Interstate 20. It provides access to Riverbanks Zoo.</li>
</ul>
