<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city and its surroundings are served by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Columbia Metropolitan Airport">Columbia Metropolitan Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CAE</b>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KCAE</b>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>CAE</b>). The airport itself is serviced by <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="American Eagle Airlines">American Eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Express</a> airlines. In addition, the city is also served by the much smaller <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hamilton%E2%80%93L.B._Owens_Airport" title="Jim Hamilton–L.B. Owens Airport">Jim Hamilton–L.B. Owens Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CUB</b>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KCUB</b>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>CUB</b>) located in the Rosewood neighborhood. It serves as the county airport for Richland County and offers <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_rail">Intercity rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Intercity rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city is served daily by <a href="/wiki/Columbia_station_(South_Carolina)" title="Columbia station (South Carolina)">Amtrak station</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Service" title="Silver Service">Silver Star</a> trains connecting Columbia with New York City, Washington, DC, <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tampa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tampa">Tampa</a>, and Miami. The station is located at 850 Pulaski St.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_bus">Intercity bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Intercity bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound Lines</a> formerly operated a station on Gervais Street, in the eastern part of downtown, providing Columbia with intercity bus transportation. The station relocated to 710 Buckner Road in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=MegaBus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MegaBus (page does not exist)">MegaBus</a> began operations in Columbia in 2015. There routes include stops in <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville, North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_DC" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington, DC">Washington, DC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="New York City, New York">New York City, New York</a>. The station is located on Sumter Street.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Sisters of Charity Providence Hospitals is sponsored by the Sisters of Charity of Saint Augustine (CSA) Health System. The non-profit organization is licensed for 304 beds and comprises four entities: Providence Hospital, Providence Heart Institute, Providence Hospital Northeast, and Providence Orthopaedic &amp; NeuroSpine Institute. Providence Hospital, located in downtown Columbia, was founded by the Sisters of Charity of Saint Augustine in 1938. The facility offers cardiac care through Providence Heart Institute, which is considered a quality cardiac center in South Carolina. Providence Hospital Northeast is a 46-bed community hospital established in 1999 that offers a range of medical services in surgery, emergency care, women's and children's services, and rehabilitation. Providence Northeast is home to Providence Orthopaedic &amp; NeuroSpine Institute, which provides medical and surgical treatment of diseases and injuries of the bones, joints, and spine.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg/220px-PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg/330px-PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg/440px-PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1384" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PalmettoHealthBaptistHospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Health" title="Palmetto Health">Palmetto Health</a> Baptist Hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Palmetto Health is a South Carolina nonprofit public benefit corporation consisting of <a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Health_Richland" title="Palmetto Health Richland">Palmetto Health Richland</a> and Palmetto Health Baptist hospitals (2locations; 1 downtown and 1 in the Harbison area) in Columbia. Palmetto Health provides health care for nearly 70 percent of the residents of Richland County and almost 55 percent of the health care for both Richland and Lexington counties. Palmetto Health Richland is the primary teaching hospital for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina_School_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="University of South Carolina School of Medicine">University of South Carolina School of Medicine</a>. Palmetto Health Baptist recently underwent a $40 million multi-phase modernization which included 37,000 square feet (3,400&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of new construction and 81,000 square feet (7,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of renovations. The extensive health system also operates Palmetto Health Children's Hospital and <a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Health_Richland" title="Palmetto Health Richland">Palmetto Health Heart Hospital</a>, the state's first freestanding hospital dedicated solely to heart care, which opened in January 2006. The Palmetto Health South Carolina Cancer Center offers patient services at the Palmetto Health Baptist and Palmetto Health Richland campuses; both are recognized by the American College of Surgeons Commission on Cancer as a Network Cancer Program.</p>
<p>Lexington Medical Center is a network of hospitals—urgent care centers that are all located throughout <a href="/wiki/Lexington_County,_South_Carolina" title="Lexington County, South Carolina">Lexington County, South Carolina</a>. There are currently six urgent care centers located in Lexington, Irmo, Batesburg-Leesville, Swansea, and Gilbert. The main hospital is in West Columbia. LMC opened in 1971 but quickly grew into a large center that has been growing every year since its opening. Currently, the main center offers an array of services from emergency treatments to the upcoming heart center.</p>
<p>The Wm. Jennings Bryan Dorn VA Medical Center is a 216-bed facility, encompassing acute medical, surgical, psychiatric, and long-term care. The hospital provides primary, secondary, and some tertiary care.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> An affiliation is held with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina_School_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="University of South Carolina School of Medicine">University of South Carolina School of Medicine</a>, located on the hospital grounds. A sharing agreement is in place with Moncrief Army Community Hospital at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Jackson_(South_Carolina)" title="Fort Jackson (South Carolina)">Fort Jackson</a> and the 20th Medical Group at <a href="/wiki/Shaw_Air_Force_Base" title="Shaw Air Force Base">Shaw AFB</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sumter,_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sumter, SC">Sumter</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Columbia,_South_Carolina" title="List of people from Columbia, South Carolina">List of people from Columbia, South Carolina</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Columbia has been the recipient of several awards and achievements. In October 2009, Columbia was listed in U.S. News &amp; World Report as one of the best places to retire, citing location and median housing price as key contributors.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> As of July 2013 Columbia was named one of "10 Great Cities to Live In" by Kiplinger Magazine. Most recently, the city has been named a top mid-sized market in the nation for relocating families,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> as well as one of 30 communities named "America's Most <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">Livable</a> Communities," an award given by the non-profit Partners for Livable Communities.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city of Columbia has 6 <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">sister cities</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kaiserslautern" title="Kaiserslautern">Kaiserslautern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>, Germany</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania"><img alt="Romania" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>, Romania</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria"><img alt="Bulgaria" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a>, Bulgaria</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia"><img alt="Russia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Chelyabinsk" title="Chelyabinsk">Chelyabinsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelyabinsk_Oblast" title="Chelyabinsk Oblast">Chelyabinsk Oblast</a>, Russia</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana"><img alt="Ghana" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, Ghana</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Yibin" title="Yibin">Yibin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a>, China</li>
